  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_19481891-57a2-4fae-86ec-d04249f0856e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2237587941197223679">An epic and heart-rending jungle adventure from the bestselling author of Kaspar and Born to Run. For Will and his mother, going to Indonesia isn't just a holiday. It's an escape, a new start, a chance to put things behind them - things like the death of Will's father.   <span id="freeText2237587941197223679" style="display:none">An epic and heart-rending jungle adventure from the bestselling author of Kaspar and Born to Run. For Will and his mother, going to Indonesia isn't just a holiday. It's an escape, a new start, a chance to put things behind them - things like the death of Will's father. And to begin with, it seems to be just what they both needed. But then Oona, the elephant Will is riding on the beach, begins acting strangely, shying away from the sea. And that's when the tsunami comes crashing in, and Oona begins to run. Except that when the tsunami is gone, Oona just keeps on running. With nothing on his back but a shirt and nothing to sustain him but a bottle of water, Will must learn to survive deep in the jungle. Luckily, though, he's not completely alone! He's got Oona.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is simple, Will's mother is actually Indonesian. Also, Will had probably never been to an overseas country before, not that Michael Morpurgo tell<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is simple, Will's mother is actually Indonesian. Also, Will had probably never been to an overseas country before, not that Michael Morpurgo tells us about that. His mum thought that going to Indonesia could make the two of them relieved about the many stresses they are going though<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341705085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3801994810730954976">A great story about a boy, and how an elephant saves the boy's life from terrible disasters. I could always visualizing what happened. The author, Michael Morpurgo, was very descriptive in this story. I was very surprised by the end, but I loved the end just as it was. I laughed out loud many many times in this story, as well as cried one or two times. <br/><br/>The relantionship that Will, the boy, and Oona, the elephant, had was incredible. They were like best friends, and when they got seprated they al</span>
  <span id="freeText3801994810730954976" style="display:none">A great story about a boy, and how an elephant saves the boy's life from terrible disasters. I could always visualizing what happened. The author, Michael Morpurgo, was very descriptive in this story. I was very surprised by the end, but I loved the end just as it was. I laughed out loud many many times in this story, as well as cried one or two times. <br /><br />The relantionship that Will, the boy, and Oona, the elephant, had was incredible. They were like best friends, and when they got seprated they always found their ways back to each other with much effort. I really wanted to be with Will and Oona through their journeys. After I finsihed the book, I missed Oona and Will. <br /><br />This story somewhat changed the way I look at life. Their are many struggles, but with friends and family you can and will make it.<br /><br />I also loved Charlie, Tonk, and Bart. They depened on Will, and Will was always there for them. He helped them through every moment of there struggles. <br /><br />The Other One, after you read the book, you will know exactly who this is, turned out to save their lives. The Other One lead them to safety and away from the fires.<br /><br />The whole book is great! I absolutely reccomend it to all readers!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3801994810730954976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2529740062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2529740062" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84847333-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2529740062?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/84847333-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2529740062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer593715080337830912">Running wild is a children’s adventure fiction novel. In this novel the story of a young boy named Will is told through captivating chapters. The emotion throughout the novel is strong and the narrative holds deeper conceptual meanings. <br/>Will and his mother are on a trip to Indonesia, Will is living out his dream of rising an elephant, when suddenly they become separated(by the elephant) in an urgent commotion. The boxing day tsunami was coming. Oona, the elephant saved Wills life from a terrible</span>
  <span id="freeText593715080337830912" style="display:none">Running wild is a children’s adventure fiction novel. In this novel the story of a young boy named Will is told through captivating chapters. The emotion throughout the novel is strong and the narrative holds deeper conceptual meanings. <br />Will and his mother are on a trip to Indonesia, Will is living out his dream of rising an elephant, when suddenly they become separated(by the elephant) in an urgent commotion. The boxing day tsunami was coming. Oona, the elephant saved Wills life from a terrible disaster, and continues to do so throughout the narrative. With the rich, vivid adjectives the visualisation of each event Will encounters is unexplainable. <br />This novel made me laugh and cry from start to finish. I was truly captivated and unable to put it down. The approachable manner in which this is achieved, through the eyes of nine-year-old Will means this book, although will have differing effects on each audience member, is accessible for KS2 pupils and above. <br />The relationship that Will, the boy, and Oona, the elephant, had was incredible. When Will and Oona got separated they always found their ways back to each other with much effort. The deeper conceptual deductions from their relationship can be taken beyond text level, and puts your own relationships, and our relationship with the animals on this planet into perspective. There are many struggles in our own lives, but with friends and family you can and will make it- just live Oona and Will (eventually) did.<br />As the book progresses, it tackles issues of poaching, deforestation, loss and despair and teaches young readers the basics of what is happening to our rainforests and its creatures.<br /><br />There are limitless opportunities for using this book in the classroom, for example:<br />English: In my SBT1 class, this book was used to assist pupils in writing persuasive pieces to stop deforestation for palm oil- pupils were captivated and passionate due to their intense emotional response to Wills story. Additionally, this novel would prove engaging should you stop just before the ending and allow pupils to continue the narrative and write their own ending(or do the same at any point of the book).<br />Science: A conceptual introduction to natural disasters and their human effects. A conceptual introduction to human disasters(deforestation for business) and their effects on humans, habitats, global warming and animals.<br />PSHE: Sections of the book could provide for good discussion topics- requiring pupils to deduct deeper meanings behind Wills feelings and relate this to their own experiences. Pupils can then share and discuss with peers. <br />Geography: This novel provides deep description and context for rainforest topics. Pupils would be better able to imagine the different layers of the rainforest, understanding the different animals and their struggles. Pupils could use self-chosen extracts of the book to add vivid description to rainforest work/projects. <br />Drama: Due to the emotive, vivid language pupils will have every enthusiasm to act out any element of this narrative. The characterisation modelled will ensure pupils can fully take on characters and paint a full picture of their traits. Hot seating from this book was observed on SBT1 and pupils responses to ‘how might ___ character be feeling in this section’ were in depth and well placed to the characters specific traits- as pupils had so many examples to relate to. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="593715080337830912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1890281488" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890281488" />
    <a title="Dafna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59161495-dafna"><img alt="Dafna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1890281488?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dafna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dafna" href="/user/show/59161495-dafna">Dafna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1890281488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12289587976939622090">Running Wild by Michael Morpurgo Is a book about a boy named Will. Will has lost his father and is still recovering, to escape from all the sadness Will and his mom take a trip to Indonesia. The elephant, Oona, Will was riding starts moving away from the beach as if she was scared. Faster than Will is able to realize a tsunami comes crashing in and Oona begins to run towards the jungle. This book is a story about how Will has to survive in the jungle with nothing but his companion, Oona.<br/> <br/>I reall</span>
  <span id="freeText12289587976939622090" style="display:none">Running Wild by Michael Morpurgo Is a book about a boy named Will. Will has lost his father and is still recovering, to escape from all the sadness Will and his mom take a trip to Indonesia. The elephant, Oona, Will was riding starts moving away from the beach as if she was scared. Faster than Will is able to realize a tsunami comes crashing in and Oona begins to run towards the jungle. This book is a story about how Will has to survive in the jungle with nothing but his companion, Oona.<br /> <br />I really enjoy Michael Morpurgo's story lines, most of them are adventurous and emotional making his books good reads. I think his style of writing is also very descriptive making his books engaging and entertaining. <br /> <br />This book was recommended in class by a friend, She said she found the book emotional but said the start was uninteresting. I completely agree with both opinions, the start of the book was uninteresting as there was no action because all the characters were being introduced. However, Will's survival adds adventure and excitement to the book and the bond that Will creates with Oona is heart melting. Although it was quite sad I really enjoyed the thrill and mix of emotions in this book.<br /> <br />Overall I think this book is great and will leave readers in tears, I recommend this book to every age and every type of reader!<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393162562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12568058630770416393">I always thought if I were ever going to have an animal for a best friend it would be a unicorn. That’s until I was introduced to Oona. The world’s most devoted, caring and intelligent Elephant, and the best friend Will could ask for. <br/><br/>I should probably warn you that this book is the tear jerker of all tear jerkers. If you’re a fan of Morpurgo then this will come as no surprise. The man sure does have a knack for dealing with sensitive subject matter. The issues dealt with in Running Wild are poi</span>
  <span id="freeText12568058630770416393" style="display:none">I always thought if I were ever going to have an animal for a best friend it would be a unicorn. That’s until I was introduced to Oona. The world’s most devoted, caring and intelligent Elephant, and the best friend Will could ask for. <br /><br />I should probably warn you that this book is the tear jerker of all tear jerkers. If you’re a fan of Morpurgo then this will come as no surprise. The man sure does have a knack for dealing with sensitive subject matter. The issues dealt with in Running Wild are poignant and almost far too real; the Iraq war, deforestation, endangered animals, and 2004’s devastating Tsunami are all brought to life in this tale of one boy overcoming all the odds to survive.<br /><br />The approachable manner in which this is achieved, through the eyes of nine year old Will, make it a truly remarkable read. Beautifully told and illustrated likewise, it is an absolute pleasure to read. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.neverendinglibrary.com/2012/08/16/running-wild-by-michael-morpurgo/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read more here...</a><br /><br /><i>The Never-Ending Library is run by HarperCollins Publishers Ltd employees about the HarperCollins Publishers Ltd books that we have read and love.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12568058630770416393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

After a few days it dawns on him that he has lost his mum, as well as his dad. He starts to make friends with the Elephant and tries to communicate using some type of sign language, unfortunately the Elephant would only stop when it was hungry and tired. While in the woods the boy gets used to his surroundings and also makes friends with the animals.<br />He gets really ill and collapses, the Elephant takes him to a place to stay and he gets treated kindly. His grandparents get called and he has to start getting used to his life without his parents which is hard!</span>

  <span id="freeText3630651164391784259" style="display:none">Running wild is a young adult novel based on events that have and are happening. As stated at the end 'it is a book that everyone in the world should know because its full of hope and determination.'<br /><br />When i first started this book i thought it would be a drag, the first twelve pages were about a train journey. However the story slowly progressed and i found i couldnt put it down. <br />After sensing a tsunami Oona an elephant that Will was riding carries him off into the jungle far away till she feels safe. Will survives in the jungle with an elephant and orangutans using instinct and the environment to stay alive. <br /><br />the story tackles the issues of poaching, deforestation, loss and despair and teaches young readers the basic of what is happening to our rainforests and its creatures, always with hope and determination that things can change. <br /><br />A heart touching story that is sometimes sad but well worth the read! </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246326816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2515105994769130653">Im an in love with this book! I usually don't like to read realistic fiction and find it boring or very descriptive about literally EVERYTHING. However, this book started off with a bang. Tragedy struck his life then instead of writing the whole book around the fact that that it happened (like I had thought it would) but it surprises you and the book comes back and slaps you across the face. Then, just as a sense of peace and tranquil comes over the characters, the book reaches out and slaps you</span>
  <span id="freeText2515105994769130653" style="display:none">Im an in love with this book! I usually don't like to read realistic fiction and find it boring or very descriptive about literally EVERYTHING. However, this book started off with a bang. Tragedy struck his life then instead of writing the whole book around the fact that that it happened (like I had thought it would) but it surprises you and the book comes back and slaps you across the face. Then, just as a sense of peace and tranquil comes over the characters, the book reaches out and slaps you in the face again. This book has kept me on my toes for every waking moment. I find myself racing towards it, bracing myself for the next slap. Reading this book is like dancing with a tiger, a continuous cycle of shocking moments, dodging, and gasping. I would defiantly recommend this book to everyone, even if you don't like this genre please read it. Thank you to Laura for recommending this book to me! </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3308855496?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Akshata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Akshata" href="/user/show/65866752-akshata">Akshata</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3308855496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11632878200158678085">This story was so enticing, and I totally loved it. Will and his mother go on a holiday in Indonesia to relax and have some fun, and that’s where it all starts. I don’t want to give too much away, but hen I was reading it I felt a mixture of lots of feelings. Sometimes it was sad, cute, funny, shocking, pleasant or surprising. And I was encouraged even more to read it - I actually found this out at the very end, but anyway - because it is a true story. What’s more, Micheal Morpurgo is the grandf</span>
  <span id="freeText11632878200158678085" style="display:none">This story was so enticing, and I totally loved it. Will and his mother go on a holiday in Indonesia to relax and have some fun, and that’s where it all starts. I don’t want to give too much away, but hen I was reading it I felt a mixture of lots of feelings. Sometimes it was sad, cute, funny, shocking, pleasant or surprising. And I was encouraged even more to read it - I actually found this out at the very end, but anyway - because it is a true story. What’s more, Micheal Morpurgo is the grandfather of the main character in the story! He wrote it in the perspective of his grandson, and that makes it even more realistic. I would rate this book even more than 5 stars if I could, and recommend it to anyone aged 9-12.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11632878200158678085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2631528597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2631528597" />
    <a title="Tianen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90739073-tianen"><img alt="Tianen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545877854p2/90739073.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2631528597?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tianen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tianen" href="/user/show/90739073-tianen">Tianen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90739073-tianen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2631528597&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2631528597" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1652885217646934786">8"The elephant lifted her trunk and began trumpeting at the sea. She swung around, and I held on for dear life as she stampeded into the shadows of the jungle..."<br/><br/>For Will and his mother, going to Indonesia isn’t just a holiday. It’s an escape, a new start, a chance to put things behind them - things like the death of Will’s father. And to begin with, it seems to be just what they both needed. But then Oona, the elephant Will is riding on the beach, begins acting strangely, shying away from the s</span>
  <span id="freeText1652885217646934786" style="display:none">8"The elephant lifted her trunk and began trumpeting at the sea. She swung around, and I held on for dear life as she stampeded into the shadows of the jungle..."<br /><br />For Will and his mother, going to Indonesia isn’t just a holiday. It’s an escape, a new start, a chance to put things behind them - things like the death of Will’s father. And to begin with, it seems to be just what they both needed. But then Oona, the elephant Will is riding on the beach, begins acting strangely, shying away from the sea. And that’s when the tsunami comes crashing in, and Oona begins to run. Except that when the tsunami is gone, Oona just keeps on running. With nothing on his back but a shirt and nothing to sustain him but a bottle of water, Will must learn to survive deep in the jungle. Luckily, though, he’s not completely alone... He’s got Oona.<br /><br />Finding this book at a bookstore and buying it for 15 dollars was definitely not regretted. I loved everything about this book! Firstly, the interesting yet tough adventure of a young boy and an elephant was just so thrilling and exciting. The fact that I could finish almost half the book without getting distracted shows how captivating the content in the book was. <br /><br />The second reason why this book is such a frigging good read is due to the heartwarming relationship formed between Oona (the elephant) and Will. I could deeply feel and connect with the emotions Will and Oona felt for each other, with Will depending heavily on Oona to survive the dangerous jungle. <br /><br />The entire book was basically about Oona and Will's intimate relationship, with Oona in her comfort zone whereas Will is struggling to survive. The book was short and sweet, with a plot which took of really quickly. The whole plot was so interesting that I could hardly identify a climax. Every single adventure in the jungle from meeting a tiger, to rescuing baby orang-utans was painted so vividly that I was entertained every single chapter. <br /><br />One of the most prominent concepts in this book was that of altruism. The revolving presence of unselfishness could be seen almost everywhere, from Oona protecting Will from dangers, keeping him alive by showing him food or water to Will generously giving the baby orang-utans his food when being held captive by the hunters. I personally feel that the element of altruism in characters such as Will and Oona creates a contrast against the selfish hunters who kill animals for their own l separate personalities of mankind can be portrayed clearly in this book through the main characters, Will, Oona and the hunters. <br /><br />All in all, this book is one of the best i have ever read, with many significances to our daily lives (read for yourself to find out!). I could not find anything i disliked in the book as well. Highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1652885217646934786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nadia Nazaruddin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72437358-nadia-nazaruddin"><img alt="Nadia Nazaruddin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543066790p2/72437358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2659145996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2632075903724892645">This book is a children adventure fiction - it meant for a children's reading so, don't expect to be much more thriller. I love this book and I enjoyed reading this. <br/><br/>It'a about a young boy named Will, who lost his father in Iraq's war and also had lost his mother in Tsunami 2004 in Indonesia. He was very young when these tragic events hit him. He was being saved by an elephant during the Tsunami and that's where his adventure begin.<br/><br/>Right after his father's death, they (Will and his mother) flew </span>
  <span id="freeText2632075903724892645" style="display:none">This book is a children adventure fiction - it meant for a children's reading so, don't expect to be much more thriller. I love this book and I enjoyed reading this. <br /><br />It'a about a young boy named Will, who lost his father in Iraq's war and also had lost his mother in Tsunami 2004 in Indonesia. He was very young when these tragic events hit him. He was being saved by an elephant during the Tsunami and that's where his adventure begin.<br /><br />Right after his father's death, they (Will and his mother) flew to Indonesia for holiday. And it is suppose to be a happy and meaningful holiday for both of them, to restart their lives without a father and a husband. When both of them were at the beach, taking their sweet time enjoying the sea, something came on. Will's mother was swimming in the sea when the tidal wave came and hit the beach. While, Will was riding on the elephant. Somehow, the elephant almost knew something bad is coming and before the tidal wave came, the elephant ran into the jungle, ran as fast as it could, as far as it could with Will still stuck on it. <br /><br />So, Will survived. He made friends with the animals in the jungle. He began to communicate with the elephant which was called Oona. He met with the tiger and orang utans. He survived by eating fruits (mostly figs) and slept in a nest (he made it on his own) on top of the tree. For almost a year he'd been living with the wild in the forest and he survived. <br /><br />One day, the forest was on fire. Oona carried him and ran as fast as she could. So did the Orang Utans. Until they came to a sanctuary - The orang utans sanctuary that was lead by a doctor named Dr. Geraldine. She has helped him a lot. She knew him. She knew his story. Because, she had a pamphlet that was given to her by Will's grandparents during their searching. But Will's heart is with the forest, with Oona and the orang utans - Bart, Tonk, Charlie, Mani and the Other One. He couldn't leave all of them. Thus, he made his mind to stay with Dr. Geraldine, and not to follow his grandparents back to England where he came from. <br /><br />It was such a heartbreaking story. I cried for a few times, especially at the beginning and the ending of the story. It's like reading a true story, a real experience. And also, to tell us that the wild and the forest need to be preserved. I would recommend to all of you to read this. Bravo!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2632075903724892645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2332607501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2332607501" />
    <a title="Eleanor Bishop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79585682-eleanor-bishop"><img alt="Eleanor Bishop" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2332607501?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eleanor Bishop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eleanor Bishop" href="/user/show/79585682-eleanor-bishop">Eleanor Bishop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2332607501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12104482176989586203">Key Themes: <br/>Respect for the environment<br/>Relationships <br/>Grief <br/><br/>My thoughts and reactions:<br/>1. Children's literature often forces its protagonists to depend upon their own resources and initiative. However, Running Wild offers a different preconception. Morpurgo tells to great effect, a story of a boy who is saved by an elephant during a tsunami. The plot follows Will, who is riding an elephant, Oona who sensed immediate danger and ran into the jungle, terrified and explores the theme of survival.<br/>2. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText12104482176989586203" style="display:none">Key Themes: <br />Respect for the environment<br />Relationships <br />Grief <br /><br />My thoughts and reactions:<br />1. Children's literature often forces its protagonists to depend upon their own resources and initiative. However, Running Wild offers a different preconception. Morpurgo tells to great effect, a story of a boy who is saved by an elephant during a tsunami. The plot follows Will, who is riding an elephant, Oona who sensed immediate danger and ran into the jungle, terrified and explores the theme of survival.<br />2. This book is told in first person, and readers who notice that Will has an improbable degree of self-awareness for a nine-year-old ("From now on I would remember only the marvellous times, the magical moments that I knew would lift my spirits, that would banish all grieving") and precocious powers of expression ("Whatever it was had transformed her from a ponderous creature of supreme gentleness and serenity, into a wild beast, maddened by terror") will find an explanation in the short postscript.<br />3. Running Wild appears to have parallel connections to Rudyard Kipling’s “The Jungle Book”, but the presentation of human life in Morpurgo’s writing is more threatening. This is perhaps because tragedy is a predominant theme in this piece of children’s literature which is demonstrated through the destruction of the environment that has arisen from human interference. <br /><br />Using this book in the classroom:<br />Running Wild can be used in the classroom by exploring the 2004 Indonesian tsunami, from which the story is based upon. This can be explored cross curricular. For example, in geography children could look at what the causes of tsunamis are and use atlases to locate places around the world that are most effected by the use of these waves. Running wild can also be analysed in guided reading sessions which can lead onto comprehension based activities involving the poem “The Tyger” by William Blake. Running Wild can also be explored in art by analysing different types of weather using different media as well as recreating the famous “The Great Wave” by Japanese artist Katsushika Hokusai. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12104482176989586203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3384494848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3384494848" />
    <a title="John  Trident " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66534748-john-trident"><img alt="John  Trident " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526706124p2/66534748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3384494848?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John  Trident " class="user" itemprop="url" name="John  Trident " href="/user/show/66534748-john-trident">John  Trident </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3384494848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3697016049635745787">An absolute gem, pageturner, relevant, important & moving novel, most of all - one of a kind! <br/><br/>I read this long ago however, I felt like sharing it now because of the recent elephant slaughter in kerala which shook our entire nation to it's core. It's very sad to see all the turmoil & atrocities innocent animals face at the hands of so-called humans living in great societies. This incident has also showed the world that literacy doesn't account for humanity. It has shed light upon the fact that t</span>
  <span id="freeText3697016049635745787" style="display:none">An absolute gem, pageturner, relevant, important &amp; moving novel, most of all - one of a kind! <br /><br />I read this long ago however, I felt like sharing it now because of the recent elephant slaughter in kerala which shook our entire nation to it's core. It's very sad to see all the turmoil &amp; atrocities innocent animals face at the hands of so-called humans living in great societies. This incident has also showed the world that literacy doesn't account for humanity. It has shed light upon the fact that though a person maybe 'highly educated', it's regardless if he turns out to be a heartless bartard inhuman - then what's the whole point of such a society, sect, religion, city or even a state like that. In the end, everything is pointless if you as a human being can't sustain to live in peace &amp; harmony with all the living creatures inhabiting this planet! <br /><br />This is an epic yet heart-rending jungle adventure for both kids &amp; adults everywhere. <br />For Will and his mother, going to Indonesia isn't just a holiday. It's an escape, a new start, a chance to put things behind them – things like the death of Will's father.<br />To begin with, it seems to be just what they both needed. But then Oona, the elephant Will is riding on the beach, begins acting strangely, shying away from the sea. That's when the tsunami comes crashing in &amp; Oona begins to run. Except that when the tsunami is gone, Oona just keeps on running.<br />With nothing on his back but a shirt &amp; nothing to sustain him but a bottle of water, Will must learn to survive deep in the jungle. Luckily, though, he's not completely alone…<br />He's got Oona.<br /><br />I loved reading this book a lot. Especially the part when how in the end it includes a complete synopsis about tsunamis &amp; world issues that aren't addressed enough. I don't think anybody would ponder upon such crucial facts with so much interest if the story wasn't so captivating, heartwrecking, heartbreaking, heart-warming &amp; touching. Let's not forget the poem 'Tyger Tyger' by William Blake. It makes this book absolutely remarkable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3697016049635745787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2854471683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2854471683" />
    <a title="Laura Saunders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98411825-laura-saunders"><img alt="Laura Saunders" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2854471683?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Saunders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Saunders" href="/user/show/98411825-laura-saunders">Laura Saunders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2854471683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5920927008176733985">A sad start to the story as the reader learns that Will a young boy has lost his Father who was a soldier at war. In order to try and recover from this his Mother takes him away. Unfortunately another major disaster befalls the young boy, as the island is hit by a massive Tsunami, whilst he is enjoying a ride on an elephant. Morpurgo basis this on a real life Tsunami that took place in 2010 killing many people and destroying the homes and livelihoods of thousands. The elephant has some sort of p</span>
  <span id="freeText5920927008176733985" style="display:none">A sad start to the story as the reader learns that Will a young boy has lost his Father who was a soldier at war. In order to try and recover from this his Mother takes him away. Unfortunately another major disaster befalls the young boy, as the island is hit by a massive Tsunami, whilst he is enjoying a ride on an elephant. Morpurgo basis this on a real life Tsunami that took place in 2010 killing many people and destroying the homes and livelihoods of thousands. The elephant has some sort of premonition/warning using his animal instincts that the Tsunami is coming and runs for the hills with, Will on his back. Whilst they escaped the Tsunami Will is now truly alone except for the elephant, having now lost his other parent to the Tsunami. He finds himself in the jungle with the elephant and nothing else , facing the daily challenges of trying to survive. The Elephant and will seem to build a close relationship and understanding of each other. unfortunately he was captured and imprisoned by an illegal business man profiteering from deforestation for the production of oil. Luckily he manages to escape from this situation with help and found himself with OOna the elephant at a sanctuary for Orangutans. He had early in the book befriended some baby orangutans and now found himself assisting at the sanctuary. Ultimately his Grandparents were contacted back in England and came out to meet him to take him home. However by now he was so accustomed to this life he no longer wanted to leave. Morpurgo finishes the book on a high with the Grandparents agreeing to join him in the sanctuary and continue with the good work. The powerful story lines of love and loss whilst incorporating freedom, nature and the preservation of the natural habitats grip the reader to the end knowing especially that the story is based on some real facts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5920927008176733985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iIAb+WoFMbpFMf1D4RmkCOXvmlGhxNqDFnY/gpH5K5iOFC9Az1jBx2H0V7XWMscBocz+eFOM7ij25jVB+DQEEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CuxtGhnEJEGXpsEh4YntJyynJULKAbJScExE/lL6uNAMeFmjvJnUPLNja9fWoo4uaIRBazhJhvmQ3E49OzeXWA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8080.Michael_Morpurgo">About Michael Morpurgo</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8080.Michael_Morpurgo"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1260905000p3/8080.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8080.Michael_Morpurgo">Michael Morpurgo
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,053
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2497925559911441612">Sir Michael Andrew Morpurgo, OBE, FRSL is the author of many books for children, five of which have been made into films. He also writes his own screenplays and libretti for opera. Born in St Albans, Hertfordshire, in 1943, he was evacuated to Cumberland during the last years of the Second World War, then returned to London, moving later to Essex. After a brief and unsuccessful spell in the army, </span>
  <span id="freeText2497925559911441612" style="display:none">Sir Michael Andrew Morpurgo, OBE, FRSL is the author of many books for children, five of which have been made into films. He also writes his own screenplays and libretti for opera. Born in St Albans, Hertfordshire, in 1943, he was evacuated to Cumberland during the last years of the Second World War, then returned to London, moving later to Essex. After a brief and unsuccessful spell in the army, he took up teaching and started to write. He left teaching after ten years in order to set up 'Farms for City Children' with his wife. They have three farms in Devon, Wales and Gloucestershire, open to inner city school children who come to stay and work with the animals. In 1999 this work was publicly recognised when he and his wife were invested a Member of the Order of the British Empire (MBE) for services to youth. In 2003, he was advanced to an Officer of the Order of the British Empire (OBE). He became a Fellow of the Royal Society of Literature (FRSL) in 2004. He was knighted in the 2018 for his services to literature and charity. He is also a father and grandfather, so children have always played a large part in his life. Every year he and his family spend time in the Scilly Isles, the setting for three of his books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2497925559911441612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
